<div id="review_3054077668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3054077668" />
    <a title="Benoit Lelièvre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3634428-benoit-leli-vre"><img alt="Benoit Lelièvre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566838000p2/3634428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3054077668?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benoit Lelièvre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benoit Lelièvre" href="/user/show/3634428-benoit-leli-vre">Benoit Lelièvre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9780007378814" href="/book/show/19053322-cocaine-nights">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3054077668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10670094998801192745">The master doing what he does best: using the rigid structure of genre fiction to question the culture it was born from and all its excesses.<br/><br/>In Cocaine Nights, Ballard uses mystery tropes to explore the weird, terrifying and sun-soaked universe of the elites living in resort towns and gated communities. Although the mystery aspects of Cocaine Nights can get pretty run-of-the-mill, they're confined to the first half of the novel and completely disappear once the narrator Charles starts living the</span>
  <span id="freeText10670094998801192745" style="display:none">The master doing what he does best: using the rigid structure of genre fiction to question the culture it was born from and all its excesses.<br /><br />In Cocaine Nights, Ballard uses mystery tropes to explore the weird, terrifying and sun-soaked universe of the elites living in resort towns and gated communities. Although the mystery aspects of Cocaine Nights can get pretty run-of-the-mill, they're confined to the first half of the novel and completely disappear once the narrator Charles starts living the life of his brother Frank and starts understanding the mechanics of Estrella De Mar community. It then beautiful a true blue Ballard novel in all its glorious weirdness. <br /><br />The underlying awfulness of wealthy people is a recurring theme in Ballard's fiction, because their well-guarded lifestyle leads to the utmost terrifying forms of freedom and they are in full display in Cocaine Nights! One of my top 5 Ballards.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10670094998801192745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2184990425?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosemary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosemary" href="/user/show/4723954-rosemary">Rosemary</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4723954-rosemary?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184990425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4866169646986807903">Charles Prentice goes to the Spanish resort of Estrella Del Mar to see his brother, who has inexplicably confessed to a crime nobody believes he committed—an arson that killed four people. But nothing in Estrella Del Mar is simple, and soon Charles is both repulsed and drawn into the closed society of expatriates where his brother seems to have been happy.<br/><br/>This is like a milder version of Crash—not that what happens is less serious, but it’s not repeated and not described in real time. I didn’t f</span>
  <span id="freeText4866169646986807903" style="display:none">Charles Prentice goes to the Spanish resort of Estrella Del Mar to see his brother, who has inexplicably confessed to a crime nobody believes he committed—an arson that killed four people. But nothing in Estrella Del Mar is simple, and soon Charles is both repulsed and drawn into the closed society of expatriates where his brother seems to have been happy.<br /><br />This is like a milder version of Crash—not that what happens is less serious, but it’s not repeated and not described in real time. I didn’t find it horrible in the same way. But it does have something of the same theme, a group of people fascinated by pushing way beyond the boundaries of morality.<br /><br />It’s slow in a dreamy way that reflects the spell the place and its inhabitants are casting on Charles, but I found it starting to drag into the second half.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4866169646986807903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_871944455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871944455" />
    <a title="Katie Grainger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5854671-katie-grainger"><img alt="Katie Grainger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311368381p2/5854671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/871944455?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Grainger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Grainger" href="/user/show/5854671-katie-grainger">Katie Grainger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006550648" href="/book/show/862090.Cocaine_Nights">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer871944455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1125333089096315839">J G Ballard likes to focus on small communities and how they function, this theme can be seen in a number of the books he writes. In Cocaine Nights the focus falls on a small Spanish resort in which an awful crime has taken place.<br/><br/>Five deaths have taken place in a horrific house fire and Frank Prentice has confessed to the crime. When his brother arrived Charles arrives at Estrella De Mar determined to discover who started the fire. However the longer Charles stays at Estrella De Mar the more he </span>
  <span id="freeText1125333089096315839" style="display:none">J G Ballard likes to focus on small communities and how they function, this theme can be seen in a number of the books he writes. In Cocaine Nights the focus falls on a small Spanish resort in which an awful crime has taken place.<br /><br />Five deaths have taken place in a horrific house fire and Frank Prentice has confessed to the crime. When his brother arrived Charles arrives at Estrella De Mar determined to discover who started the fire. However the longer Charles stays at Estrella De Mar the more he is seduced by the place and the desire to find the truth begins to slip away. <br /><br />I thought this was quite a fascinating study on small communities and how they function. It provides an interesting philosophy on people and relationships as well as having an intriguing mystery element. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1125333089096315839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3026712681" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3026712681?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AnnaG" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AnnaG" href="/user/show/62187194-annag">AnnaG</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9780007378814" href="/book/show/19053322-cocaine-nights">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62187194-annag?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62187194-annag?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62187194-annag?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62187194-annag?shelf=dreadful">dreadful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3026712681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2759757782038965917">This is a bizarre mix-up of a book. The setting and premise of the story remind me of an Agatha Christie, where our protagonist goes to solve a mystery in sunny climes, but unlike in those stories - there are no compelling characters to meet along the way, no real revelations of what happened & why and no progression of a plot to a conclusion. Instead we just wander into a smutty and seedy world and then sort of wander out again... Not for me...</span>
  <span id="freeText2759757782038965917" style="display:none">This is a bizarre mix-up of a book. The setting and premise of the story remind me of an Agatha Christie, where our protagonist goes to solve a mystery in sunny climes, but unlike in those stories - there are no compelling characters to meet along the way, no real revelations of what happened &amp; why and no progression of a plot to a conclusion. Instead we just wander into a smutty and seedy world and then sort of wander out again... Not for me...</span>
  <a data-text-id="2759757782038965917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EcTnaYFwPliJAtI7NfEOVqi8bELaRMQFkE+GJbGnfPn2gEbMJ0WohJGanP0aAXpOc1lYui7/11ihUWVbfkNZ/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QwOQkjlcqwhv+idJJeSAIEbQn2XYhfimFOMGF7OSdoOkRzE3n2k91HdiaY8KFPQ4nTWrnSw+6/sl/eVpfHZThQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7010931.J_G_Ballard">About J.G. Ballard</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7010931.J_G_Ballard"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1497551843p3/7010931.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7010931.J_G_Ballard">J.G. Ballard
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,610
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9306065953133648693">James Graham "J. G." Ballard (15 November 1930 – 19 April 2009) was an English novelist, short story writer, and essayist. Ballard came to be associated with the New Wave of science fiction early in his career with apocalyptic (or post-apocalyptic) novels such as <i>The Drowned World</i> (1962), <i>The Burning World</i> (1964), and <i>The Crystal World</i> (1966). In the late 1960s and early 1970s Ballard focused on a</span>
  <span id="freeText9306065953133648693" style="display:none">James Graham "J. G." Ballard (15 November 1930 – 19 April 2009) was an English novelist, short story writer, and essayist. Ballard came to be associated with the New Wave of science fiction early in his career with apocalyptic (or post-apocalyptic) novels such as <i>The Drowned World</i> (1962), <i>The Burning World</i> (1964), and <i>The Crystal World</i> (1966). In the late 1960s and early 1970s Ballard focused on an eclectic variety of short stories (or "condensed novels") such as <i>The Atrocity Exhibition</i> (1970), which drew closer comparison with the work of postmodernist writers such as William S. Burroughs. In 1973 the highly controversial novel <i>Crash</i> was published, a story about symphorophilia and car crash fetishism; the protagonist becomes sexually aroused by staging and participating in real car crashes. The story was later adapted into a film of the same name by Canadian director David Cronenberg.<br /><br />While many of Ballard's stories are thematically and narratively unusual, he is perhaps best known for his relatively conventional war novel, <i>Empire of the Sun</i> (1984), a semi-autobiographical account of a young boy's experiences in Shanghai during the Second Sino-Japanese War as it came to be occupied by the Japanese Imperial Army. Described as "The best British novel about the Second World War" by <i>The Guardian</i>, the story was adapted into a 1987 film by Steven Spielberg.<br /><br />The literary distinctiveness of Ballard's work has given rise to the adjective "Ballardian", defined by the <i>Collins English Dictionary</i> as "resembling or suggestive of the conditions described in J. G. Ballard's novels and stories, especially dystopian modernity, bleak man-made landscapes and the psychological effects of technological, social or environmental developments." The <i>Oxford Dictionary of National Biography</i> entry describes Ballard's work as being occupied with "eros, thanatos, mass media and emergent technologies".</span>
  <a data-text-id="9306065953133648693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
